`public void * `[`tommy_hashdyn_remove`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a01457fa26338c432cfe9ba93da4ae2f4)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_search_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a9008971cd09a3f9c4f9da45cffb4627d)` * cmp,const void * cmp_arg,`[`tommy_hash_t`](#tommyhash_8h_1a4f9b62639e55aa933ebcf10f2125f862)` hash)`            | Searches and removes an element from the hashtable. #### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_chain_splice`](#tommychain_8h_1af8df85eb7726d2c8a7e4a6067e0f25e4)`(`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * first_before,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * first_after,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * second_head,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * second_tail)`

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_chain_concat`](#tommychain_8h_1a08a2a181678c1a6bd0ba51149e26432b)`(`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * first_tail,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * second_head)`

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_chain_merge`](#tommychain_8h_1ad5488892671ac019875b88d5746d49ae)`(`[`tommy_chain`](#tommychain_8h_1a5f4a75e4da24f984785181cb2b43efdb)` * first,`[`tommy_chain`](#tommychain_8h_1a5f4a75e4da24f984785181cb2b43efdb)` * second,`[`tommy_compare_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a2e56e0b56065d3200e65f2a5518651d0)` * cmp)` 

Merges two chains.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_chain_merge_degenerated`](#tommychain_8h_1a3dc40e721756b67836082025a4a8ba58)`(`[`tommy_chain`](#tommychain_8h_1a5f4a75e4da24f984785181cb2b43efdb)` * first,`[`tommy_chain`](#tommychain_8h_1a5f4a75e4da24f984785181cb2b43efdb)` * second,`[`tommy_compare_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a2e56e0b56065d3200e65f2a5518651d0)` * cmp)` 

Merges two chains managing special degenerated cases. It's funtionally equivalent at [tommy_chain_merge()](#tommychain_8h_1ad5488892671ac019875b88d5746d49ae) but faster with already ordered chains.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_chain_mergesort`](#tommychain_8h_1ac5bb4b7ea4bc78e882605a0407267a26)`(`[`tommy_chain`](#tommychain_8h_1a5f4a75e4da24f984785181cb2b43efdb)` * chain,`[`tommy_compare_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a2e56e0b56065d3200e65f2a5518651d0)` * cmp)` 

Sorts a chain. It's a stable merge sort using power of 2 buckets, with O(N*log(N)) complexity, similar at the one used in the SGI STL libraries and in the Linux Kernel, but faster on degenerated cases like already ordered lists.

SGI STL stl_list.h [http://www.sgi.com/tech/stl/stl_list.h](http://www.sgi.com/tech/stl/stl_list.h)

Linux Kernel lib/list_sort.c [http://lxr.linux.no/#linux+v2.6.36/lib/list_sort.c](http://lxr.linux.no/#linux+v2.6.36/lib/list_sort.c)

#### `public `[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` `[`tommy_hash_u32`](#tommyhash_8h_1ab020046d7799cda5b440bd49b4e282d8)`(`[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` init_val,const void * void_key,`[`tommy_size_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a32aad870b975610a257f9c2d14b0825e)` key_len)` 

Hash function with a 32 bits result. Implementation of the Robert Jenkins "lookup3" hash 32 bits version, from [http://www.burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/doobs.html,](http://www.burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/doobs.html,) function hashlittle(). 
#### Parameters
* `init_val` Initialization value. Using a different initialization value, you can generate a completely different set of hash values. Use 0 if not relevant. 

* `void_key` Pointer at the data to hash. 

* `key_len` Size of the data to hash. 

This function is endianess independent. 

#### Returns
The hash value of 32 bits.

#### `public `[`tommy_uint64_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a169e7168a1f2b4c01cbd525204c3be63)` `[`tommy_hash_u64`](#tommyhash_8h_1ab8bec53cea498dcff8982382c82a0695)`(`[`tommy_uint64_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a169e7168a1f2b4c01cbd525204c3be63)` init_val,const void * void_key,`[`tommy_size_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a32aad870b975610a257f9c2d14b0825e)` key_len)` 

Hash function with a 64 bits result. Implementation of the Robert Jenkins "lookup3" hash 64 bits versions, from [http://www.burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/doobs.html,](http://www.burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/doobs.html,) function hashlittle2(). 
#### Parameters
* `init_val` Initialization value. Using a different initialization value, you can generate a completely different set of hash values. Use 0 if not relevant. 

* `void_key` Pointer at the data to hash. 

* `key_len` Size of the data to hash. 

This function is endianess independent. 

#### Returns
The hash value of 64 bits.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` `[`tommy_inthash_u32`](#tommyhash_8h_1aa40f4462085f74475569e4ed298c0fc8)`(`[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` key)` 

Integer hash of 32 bits. Implementation of the Robert Jenkins "4-byte Integer Hashing", from [http://burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/integer.html](http://burtleburtle.net/bob/hash/integer.html)

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_uint64_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a169e7168a1f2b4c01cbd525204c3be63)` `[`tommy_inthash_u64`](#tommyhash_8h_1af4eccff7dd62c7f76b6522b9523775ff)`(`[`tommy_uint64_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a169e7168a1f2b4c01cbd525204c3be63)` key)` 

Integer hash of 64 bits. Implementation of the Thomas Wang "Integer Hash Function", from [http://www.cris.com/~Ttwang/tech/inthash.htm](http://www.cris.com/~Ttwang/tech/inthash.htm)

#### `public void `[`tommy_hashdyn_init`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a912bebbbb99e453f9c3230948f332d76)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn)` 

Initializes the hashtable.

#### `public void `[`tommy_hashdyn_done`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1acc92e6ad011a22aa645cb35d24df27a2)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn)` 

Deinitializes the hashtable.

You can call this function with elements still contained, but such elements are not going to be freed by this call.

#### `public void `[`tommy_hashdyn_insert`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1adef3d60ad281f391ae1032f43f584dac)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_hashdyn_node`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1aae681213ad96845453f1533ffa555481)` * node,void * data,`[`tommy_hash_t`](#tommyhash_8h_1a4f9b62639e55aa933ebcf10f2125f862)` hash)` 

Inserts an element in the hashtable.

#### `public void * `[`tommy_hashdyn_remove`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a01457fa26338c432cfe9ba93da4ae2f4)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_search_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a9008971cd09a3f9c4f9da45cffb4627d)` * cmp,const void * cmp_arg,`[`tommy_hash_t`](#tommyhash_8h_1a4f9b62639e55aa933ebcf10f2125f862)` hash)` 

Searches and removes an element from the hashtable. You have to provide a compare function and the hash of the element you want to remove. If the element is not found, 0 is returned. If more equal elements are present, the first one is removed. 
#### Parameters
* `cmp` Compare function called with cmp_arg as first argument and with the element to compare as a second one. The function should return 0 for equal elements, anything other for different elements. 

* `cmp_arg` Compare argument passed as first argument of the compare function. 

* `hash` Hash of the element to find and remove. 

#### Returns
The removed element, or 0 if not found.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_hashdyn_node`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1aae681213ad96845453f1533ffa555481)` * `[`tommy_hashdyn_bucket`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1ace3205c1f675bb98f04317c6e6574ce7)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_hash_t`](#tommyhash_8h_1a4f9b62639e55aa933ebcf10f2125f862)` hash)` 

Gets the bucket of the specified hash. The bucket is guaranteed to contain ALL the elements with the specified hash, but it can contain also others. You can access elements in the bucket following the ::next pointer until 0. 
#### Parameters
* `hash` Hash of the element to find. 

#### Returns
The head of the bucket, or 0 if empty.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void * `[`tommy_hashdyn_search`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a54558d389934ca4c412a3bc8feb76ea8)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_search_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a9008971cd09a3f9c4f9da45cffb4627d)` * cmp,const void * cmp_arg,`[`tommy_hash_t`](#tommyhash_8h_1a4f9b62639e55aa933ebcf10f2125f862)` hash)` 

Searches an element in the hashtable. You have to provide a compare function and the hash of the element you want to find. If more equal elements are present, the first one is returned. 
#### Parameters
* `cmp` Compare function called with cmp_arg as first argument and with the element to compare as a second one. The function should return 0 for equal elements, anything other for different elements. 

* `cmp_arg` Compare argument passed as first argument of the compare function. 

* `hash` Hash of the element to find. 

#### Returns
The first element found, or 0 if none.

#### `public void * `[`tommy_hashdyn_remove_existing`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a0d9f4ca17314d1a0e8b7072b5fda25cc)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_hashdyn_node`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1aae681213ad96845453f1533ffa555481)` * node)` 

Removes an element from the hashtable. You must already have the address of the element to remove. 
#### Returns
The [tommy_node::data](#structtommy__node__struct_1a6210792ec52fa1efbfb44cf4557d9b6f) field of the node removed.

#### `public void `[`tommy_hashdyn_foreach`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a010d0131e6e5ddd071dff7dadd181cfa)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_foreach_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a8caf78c4fb7706a85093f99598d61b5d)` * func)` 

Calls the specified function for each element in the hashtable.

You can use this function to deallocate all the elements inserted.

```cpp
tommy_hashdyn hashdyn;

// initializes the hashtable
tommy_hashdyn_init(&hashdyn);

...

// creates an object
struct object* obj = malloc(sizeof(struct object));

...

// insert it in the hashtable
tommy_hashdyn_insert(&hashdyn, &obj->node, obj, tommy_inthash_u32(obj->value));

...

// deallocates all the objects iterating the hashtable
tommy_hashdyn_foreach(&hashdyn, free);

// deallocates the hashtable
tommy_hashdyn_done(&hashdyn);
```

#### `public void `[`tommy_hashdyn_foreach_arg`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1af1cf2aabf2d7acd3fd78f943384aac9c)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn,`[`tommy_foreach_arg_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1ae0aea577584dfbe750f078b3801d0ee6)` * func,void * arg)` 

Calls the specified function with an argument for each element in the hashtable.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_count_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a802a296e9903e3bc098432b9bdad03ab)` `[`tommy_hashdyn_count`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a7acaf109a283cc4b8a135eaac5abf096)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn)`

#### `public `[`tommy_size_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a32aad870b975610a257f9c2d14b0825e)` `[`tommy_hashdyn_memory_usage`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a3662ac977607f8192738aa9887d70d06)`(`[`tommy_hashdyn`](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1a00c8b944d273f38f9eef91417a1e8991)` * hashdyn)` 

Gets the size of allocated memory. It includes the size of the [tommy_hashdyn_node](#tommyhashdyn_8h_1aae681213ad96845453f1533ffa555481) of the stored elements.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_list_init`](#tommylist_8h_1a2ca76ae93aeb042a70e9f8715e7b3657)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list)` 

Initializes the list. The list is completely inplace, so it doesn't need to be deinitialized.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * `[`tommy_list_head`](#tommylist_8h_1ac6075bc3125cdda1ca1efae4806188ba)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list)`

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_list_insert_head`](#tommylist_8h_1af724d44b028717ffa6b595d5cac2a73f)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * node,void * data)`

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_list_insert_tail`](#tommylist_8h_1ab84c5d58a38a05a753302279e31d2fa6)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * node,void * data)`

* `data` The object containing the node. It's used to set the [tommy_node::data](#structtommy__node__struct_1a6210792ec52fa1efbfb44cf4557d9b6f) field of the node.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * `[`tommy_list_remove_head_not_empty`](#tommylist_8h_1a927e188bc2a9959a58ff8bf6cb7c01e4)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list)` 

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void * `[`tommy_list_remove_existing`](#tommylist_8h_1aeb12015a01d368c24ce9c71c7694c6bd)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * node)` 

Removes an element from the list. You must already have the address of the element to remove. The node content is left unchanged, including the [tommy_node::next](#structtommy__node__struct_1a53338f3f5366866598ed9ac7e46e64a2) and [tommy_node::prev](#structtommy__node__struct_1a5f5ffba676428636553612ddd809443c) fields that still contain pointers at the list. 

#### Parameters
* `node` The node to remove. The node must be in the list. 

#### Returns
The [tommy_node::data](#structtommy__node__struct_1a6210792ec52fa1efbfb44cf4557d9b6f) field of the node removed.

#### `public void `[`tommy_list_concat`](#tommylist_8h_1aa23d4cbad2a1b0c9015de64dee8a95f6)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * first,`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * second)` 

Concats two lists. The second list is concatenated at the first list. 
#### Parameters
* `first` The first list. 

* `second` The second list. After this call the list content is undefined, and you should not use it anymore.

#### `public void `[`tommy_list_sort`](#tommylist_8h_1a0edd81ae314ffaccc527945a68df1165)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_compare_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a2e56e0b56065d3200e65f2a5518651d0)` * cmp)` 

Sorts a list. It's a stable merge sort with O(N*log(N)) worst complexity. It's faster on degenerated cases like partially ordered lists. 
#### Parameters
* `cmp` Compare function called with two elements. The function should return <0 if the first element is less than the second, ==0 if equal, and >0 if greather.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_bool_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1afa577fad20a7ce79f14522a0d202bc96)` `[`tommy_list_empty`](#tommylist_8h_1a251fd0bf21c3a303541ab7678679b666)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list)` 

Checks if empty. 
#### Returns
If the list is empty.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_list_foreach`](#tommylist_8h_1aac587218120cbf5bdebbb642c3550d75)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_foreach_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1a8caf78c4fb7706a85093f99598d61b5d)` * func)` 

Calls the specified function for each element in the list.

You can use this function to deallocate all the elements inserted in a list.

```cpp
tommy_list list;

// initializes the list
tommy_list_init(&list);

...

// creates an object
struct object* obj = malloc(sizeof(struct object));

...

// insert it in the list
tommy_list_insert_tail(&list, &obj->node, obj);

...

// deallocates all the objects iterating the list
tommy_list_foreach(&list, free);
```

#### `public `[`tommy_inline`](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)` void `[`tommy_list_foreach_arg`](#tommylist_8h_1a5975a58fa48d149b649fdc0f757270ba)`(`[`tommy_list`](#tommylist_8h_1a45d098412d5f0be21113b252caee491b)` * list,`[`tommy_foreach_arg_func`](#tommytypes_8h_1ae0aea577584dfbe750f078b3801d0ee6)` * func,void * arg)` 

Calls the specified function with an argument for each element in the list.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_uint_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1aeb21ea228f19971e47c8fba1023a598d)` `[`tommy_ilog2_u32`](#tommytypes_8h_1aea2d4529a17522bceaf178cc3d573ecd)`(`[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` value)` 

Bit scan reverse or integer log2. Return the bit index of the most significant 1 bit.

If no bit is set, the result is undefined. To force a return 0 in this case, you can use tommy_ilog2_u32(value | 1).

Other interesting ways for bitscan are at:

Bit Twiddling Hacks [http://graphics.stanford.edu/~seander/bithacks.html](http://graphics.stanford.edu/~seander/bithacks.html)

Chess Programming BitScan [http://chessprogramming.wikispaces.com/BitScan](http://chessprogramming.wikispaces.com/BitScan)

#### Parameters
* `value` Value to scan. 0 is not allowed. 

#### Returns
The index of the most significant bit set.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_uint_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1aeb21ea228f19971e47c8fba1023a598d)` `[`tommy_ctz_u32`](#tommytypes_8h_1ad8834ae7dab0d97eaddd1af35316fcb6)`(`[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` value)` 

Bit scan forward or trailing zero count. Return the bit index of the least significant 1 bit.

If no bit is set, the result is undefined. 
#### Parameters
* `value` Value to scan. 0 is not allowed. 

#### Returns
The index of the least significant bit set.

#### `public `[`tommy_inline](#tommytypes_8h_1afc7aaef3e7f4c50b5f723ec1683efb7d)[tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` `[`tommy_roundup_pow2_u32`](#tommytypes_8h_1a75a8e4cf1daf16cdc79fbbefb6289929)`(`[`tommy_uint32_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a21bc1d926c6dcd89e5c10fb201ee03a4)` value)` 

Rounds up to the next power of 2. For the value 0, the result is undefined. 
#### Returns
The smallest power of 2 not less than the specified value.

#### `public unsigned int `[`binToDec`](#namespacebin_op_1a5a22ca6b11e7d8241a97889523a97fdd)`(unsigned int * numBin,unsigned int binLen)` 

#### Parameters

* `binLen` length of numBin 

#### Returns
the decimal representation of the binary number

compute the next highest power of 2 of 32-bit v

# namespace `combblas` 

Connected components based on Awerbuch-Shiloach algorithm

Operations used in parallel reductions and scans

Functions that are used by multiple parallel matrix classes, but don't need the "this" pointer

`public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`PermEdges`](#namespacecombblas_1a30ccd4f66c1709d7cdb61cf88a2a9de7)`(`[`DistEdgeList`](#classcombblas_1_1_dist_edge_list)`< IT > & DEL)`            | Randomly permutes the distributed edge list. Once we call Viral's psort on this vector, everything will go to the right place [tuples are sorted lexicographically] and you can reconstruct the int64_t * edges in an embarrassingly parallel way. As I understood, the entire purpose of this function is to destroy any locality. It does not rename any vertices and edges are not named anyway. For an example, think about the edge (0,1). It will eventually (at the end of kernel 1) be owned by processor P(0,0). However, assume that processor P(r1,c1) has a copy of it before the call to PermEdges. After this call, some other irrelevant processor P(r2,c2) will own it. So we gained nothing, it is just a scrambled egg.
`public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`RenameVertices`](#namespacecombblas_1a4a5966236b5261a82b7018998432a1bf)`(`[`DistEdgeList`](#classcombblas_1_1_dist_edge_list)`< IU > & DEL)`            | Rename vertices globally. You first need to do create a random permutation distributed on all processors. Then the p round robin algorithm will do the renaming: For all processors P(i,i) Broadcast local_p to all p processors For j= i*N/p to min((i+1)*N/p, N) Rename the all j's with local_p(j) inside the edgelist (and mark them "renamed" so that yeach vertex id is renamed only once)

`public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1ab9afeed1087eca63a5e8db75f31c187d)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,NU1 Vzero,const bool useExtendedBinOp)`            | Performs an arbitrary binary operation _binary_op on the corresponding elements of two vectors with the result stored in a return vector ret. The binary operatiation is only performed if the binary predicate _doOp returns true for those elements. Otherwise the binary operation is not performed and ret does not contain an element at that position. More formally the operation is defined as: if (_doOp(V[i], W[i])) ret[i] = _binary_op(V[i], W[i]) else // ret[i] is not set Hence _doOp can be used to implement a filter on either of the vectors.

`public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`SpMXSpV_HeapSort`](#namespacecombblas_1acb3ff74ebde3c08da979fab30cdd8fb6)`(const `[`Csc`](#classcombblas_1_1_csc)`< IT, NT > & Acsc,int32_t mA,const int32_t * indx,const IVT * numx,int32_t veclen,std::vector< int32_t > & indy,std::vector< OVT > & numy,int32_t offset)`            | SpMXSpV with HeapSort Simply insert entries from columns corresponsing to nonzeros of the input vector into a minHeap Then extract entries from the minHeap Complexity: O(flops*log(flops)) offset is the offset of indices in the matrix in case the matrix is split This version is likely to be more memory efficient than the other one (the one that uses preallocated memory buffers) Because here we don't use a dense accumulation vector but a heap. It will probably be slower though.

`class `[`combblas::FullyDist`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist) | 
`class `[`combblas::FullyDist< IT, NT, typename combblas::disable_if< combblas::is_boolean< NT >::value, NT >::type >`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_3_01_i_t_00_01_n_t_00_01typename_01combblas_1_1disable__if_3_01comb0ea87b0ccc25fd3bcdc4bbc3ef87cb3e) | The full distribution is actually a two-level distribution that matches the matrix distribution In this scheme, each processor row (except the last) is responsible for t = floor(n/sqrt(p)) elements. The last processor row gets the remaining (n-floor(n/sqrt(p))*(sqrt(p)-1)) elements Within the processor row, each processor (except the last) is responsible for loc = floor(t/sqrt(p)) elements. Example: n=103 and p=16 All processors P_ij for i=0,1,2 and j=0,1,2 get floor(floor(102/4)/4) = 6 elements All processors P_i3 for i=0,1,2 get 25-6*3 = 7 elements All processors P_3j for j=0,1,2 get (102-25*3)/4 = 6 elements Processor P_33 gets 27-6*3 = 9 elements Both derived classes, whether sparse or dense, are distributed to processors based on their "length", so that a conversion does not need any communication between sparse and dense formats
`class `[`combblas::FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec) | A sparse vector of length n (with nnz <= n of them being nonzeros) is distributed to "all the processors" in a way that "respects ordering" of the nonzero indices Example: x = [5,1,6,2,9] for nnz(x)=5 and length(x)=12 we use 4 processors P_00, P_01, P_10, P_11 Then P_00 owns [1,2](in the range [0,...,2]), P_01 ow`ns [5](in the range [3,...,5]), and so on. In the case of A(v,w) type sparse matrix indexing, this doesn't matter because n = nnz After all, A(v,w) will have dimensions length(v) x length (w) v and w will be of numerical type (NT) "int" and their indices (IT) will be consecutive integers It is possibly that nonzero counts are distributed unevenly Example: x=[1,2,3,4,5] and length(x) = 20, then P_00 would own all the nonzeros and the rest will hold empry vectors Just like in [SpParMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat) case, indices are local to processors (they belong to range [0,...,length-1] on each processor) Always create vectors with the right length, setting elements won't increase its length (similar to operator[] on std::vector)

`class `[`combblas::SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat) | Fundamental 2D distributed sparse matrix class The index type IT is encapsulated by the class in a way that it is only guarantee that the implementation will ensure the requested semantics. For instance, if IT=int64 then the implementation can still use 32 bit local indices but it should return correct 64-bit numbers in its functions. In other words, DER can be SpDCCols<int32_t, double> while IT=int64_t
`class `[`combblas::SpTuples`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) | Triplets are represented using the boost::tuple class of the Boost library Number of entries are 64-bit addressible, but each entry is only <class it>=""> addressible Therefore, size is int64_t but nrows/ncols (representing range of first two entries in tuple) is of type IT Indices start from 0 in this class

`struct `[`combblas::SpImpl`](#structcombblas_1_1_sp_impl) | IT: The sparse matrix index type. Sparse vector index type is fixed to be int32_t It is the caller function's (inside ParFriends/Friends) job to convert any different types and ensure correctness. Rationale is efficiency, and the fact that we know for sure that 32-bit LOCAL indices are sufficient for all reasonable concurrencies and data sizes (as of 2011)

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`LocalSpMV`](#namespacecombblas_1ac4aa3e240fb298aafb4a9dfd1898234a)`(const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IT, bool, UDER > & A,int rowneighs,`[`OptBuf`](#classcombblas_1_1_opt_buf)`< int32_t, VT > & optbuf,int32_t *& indacc,VT *& numacc,int * sendcnt,int accnz)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IT, VT > `[`SpMV`](#namespacecombblas_1af6d7c2a1ec21df8ebdd4cff3eb728fc7)`(const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IT, bool, UDER > & A,const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IT, VT > & x,`[`OptBuf`](#classcombblas_1_1_opt_buf)`< int32_t, VT > & optbuf)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`DeleteAll`](#namespacecombblas_1a0a2526fff4629cf10a98364d57577340)`(`[`A`](#options_8h_1a2941385b1be5280d3b1f546356f7ec99)` arr1,`[`B`](#options_8h_1adf085adbf76beb194ac436d42cd1d725)` arr2,`[`C`](#options_8h_1a8987032f6f7d7cfaa0ff4e2a62ae08fe)` arr3,`[`D`](#options_8h_1ad8657a5ec76e12f3066fb4b4eb75ace9)` arr4,E arr5,F arr6)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`PermEdges`](#namespacecombblas_1a30ccd4f66c1709d7cdb61cf88a2a9de7)`(`[`DistEdgeList`](#classcombblas_1_1_dist_edge_list)`< IT > & DEL)` 

Randomly permutes the distributed edge list. Once we call Viral's psort on this vector, everything will go to the right place [tuples are sorted lexicographically] and you can reconstruct the int64_t * edges in an embarrassingly parallel way. As I understood, the entire purpose of this function is to destroy any locality. It does not rename any vertices and edges are not named anyway. For an example, think about the edge (0,1). It will eventually (at the end of kernel 1) be owned by processor P(0,0). However, assume that processor P(r1,c1) has a copy of it before the call to PermEdges. After this call, some other irrelevant processor P(r2,c2) will own it. So we gained nothing, it is just a scrambled egg.

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`RenameVertices`](#namespacecombblas_1a4a5966236b5261a82b7018998432a1bf)`(`[`DistEdgeList`](#classcombblas_1_1_dist_edge_list)`< IU > & DEL)` 

Rename vertices globally. You first need to do create a random permutation distributed on all processors. Then the p round robin algorithm will do the renaming: For all processors P(i,i) Broadcast local_p to all p processors For j= i*N/p to min((i+1)*N/p, N) Rename the all j's with local_p(j) inside the edgelist (and mark them "renamed" so that yeach vertex id is renamed only once)

#### `public inline static `[`int64_t`](#compat_8h_1a312c7e8848187d110315ab83a7b3d4d0)` `[`get_v0_from_edge`](#namespacecombblas_1ad5232de38546c1d86e9bb8cbba56d295)`(const `[`packed_edge`](#structcombblas_1_1packed__edge)` * p)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`Dcsc](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)< IU, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote > `[`EWiseMult`](#namespacecombblas_1a1fca28136b736b66fea4f09e01b199c5)`(const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU1 > & A,const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU2 > * B,bool exclude)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, N_promote > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1a17148c59f16d4908b17b807a959abcc5)`(const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU1 > & A,const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU2 > * B,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,bool notB,const NU2 & defaultBVal)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpDCCols](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)< IU, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote > `[`EWiseMult`](#namespacecombblas_1adbd747ab5c3d09bc0b2e34fd2ade32d5)`(const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU1 > & A,const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU2 > & B,bool exclude)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, N_promote > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1a138c99358a8b4eea45e087cdd4aed2e5)`(const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU1 > & A,const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU2 > & B,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,bool notB,const NU2 & defaultBVal)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, RETT > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1a21576e57b30fd67600ab7ce0d4fff414)`(const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU1 > * Ap,const `[`Dcsc`](#classcombblas_1_1_dcsc)`< IU, NU2 > * Bp,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,_BinaryPredicate do_op,bool allowANulls,bool allowBNulls,const NU1 & ANullVal,const NU2 & BNullVal,const bool allowIntersect)` 

Implementation based on operator += Element wise apply with the following constraints The operation to be performed is __binary_op The operation `c = __binary_op(a, b)` is only performed if `do_op(a, b)` returns true If allowANulls is true, then if A is missing an element that B has, then ANullVal is used In that case the operation becomes c[i,j] = __binary_op(ANullVal, b[i,j]) If both allowANulls and allowBNulls is false then the function degenerates into intersection

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, RETT > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1a7b9f3ee855e4a95fa6fbc88f0f6e6b72)`(const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU1 > & A,const `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IU, NU2 > & B,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,_BinaryPredicate do_op,bool allowANulls,bool allowBNulls,const NU1 & ANullVal,const NU2 & BNullVal,const bool allowIntersect)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NUO, UDERO > `[`Mult_AnXBn_DoubleBuff`](#namespacecombblas_1a1f6672a5752e8c99ccf217242b7f02ff)`(`[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU1, UDERA > & A,`[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU2, UDERB > & B,bool clearA,bool clearB)` 

Parallel C = A*B routine that uses a double buffered broadcasting scheme { Input matrices, A and B, should not alias } Most memory efficient version available. Total stages: 2*sqrt(p) [Memory](#classcombblas_1_1_memory) requirement during first sqrt(p) stages: <= (3/2)*(nnz(A)+nnz(B))+(1/2)*nnz(C) [Memory](#classcombblas_1_1_memory) requirement during second sqrt(p) stages: <= nnz(A)+nnz(B)+nnz(C) Final memory requirement: nnz(C) if clearA and clearB are true

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NUO, UDERO > `[`Mult_AnXBn_Synch`](#namespacecombblas_1a3efbd225dd2dc4eac01504d720ce77f8)`(`[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU1, UDERA > & A,`[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU2, UDERB > & B,bool clearA,bool clearB)` 

Parallel A = B*C routine that uses only MPI-1 features Relies on simple blocking broadcast { Input matrices, A and B, should not alias }

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)< IU, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote > `[`EWiseMult`](#namespacecombblas_1a3526276a9c54e8c69e0fd04b3e57f0f4)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,bool exclude,NU2 zero)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply_threaded`](#namespacecombblas_1a2efb4c449c210b14b8a2d500d6bdeaa0)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,NU1 Vzero,const bool useExtendedBinOp)`

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1ab9afeed1087eca63a5e8db75f31c187d)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,NU1 Vzero,const bool useExtendedBinOp)` 

Performs an arbitrary binary operation _binary_op on the corresponding elements of two vectors with the result stored in a return vector ret. The binary operatiation is only performed if the binary predicate _doOp returns true for those elements. Otherwise the binary operation is not performed and ret does not contain an element at that position. More formally the operation is defined as: if (_doOp(V[i], W[i])) ret[i] = _binary_op(V[i], W[i]) else // ret[i] is not set Hence _doOp can be used to implement a filter on either of the vectors.

The above is only defined if both V[i] and W[i] exist (i.e. an intersection). To allow a union operation (ex. when V[i] doesn't exist but W[i] does) the allowVNulls flag is set to true and the Vzero argument is used as the missing V[i] value.

The type of each element of ret must not necessarily be related to the types of V or W, so the return type must be explicitly specified as a template parameter: FullyDistSpVec<int, double> r = EWiseApply<double>(V, W, plus, retTrue, false, 0)

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1aafb55eea3daf14be805a1ccd0330d7af)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,bool allowWNulls,NU1 Vzero,NU2 Wzero,const bool allowIntersect,const bool useExtendedBinOp)` 

Performs an arbitrary binary operation _binary_op on the corresponding elements of two vectors with the result stored in a return vector ret. The binary operatiation is only performed if the binary predicate _doOp returns true for those elements. Otherwise the binary operation is not performed and ret does not contain an element at that position. More formally the operation is defined as: if (_doOp(V[i], W[i])) ret[i] = _binary_op(V[i], W[i]) else // ret[i] is not set Hence _doOp can be used to implement a filter on either of the vectors.

The above is only defined if both V[i] and W[i] exist (i.e. an intersection). To allow a union operation (ex. when V[i] doesn't exist but W[i] does) the allowVNulls flag is set to true and the Vzero argument is used as the missing V[i] value. !allowVNulls && !allowWNulls => intersection !allowVNulls && allowWNulls => operate on all elements of V allowVNulls && !allowWNulls => operate on all elements of W allowVNulls && allowWNulls => union

The type of each element of ret must not necessarily be related to the types of V or W, so the return type must be explicitly specified as a template parameter: FullyDistSpVec<int, double> r = EWiseApply<double>(V, W, plus, ...) For intersection, Vzero and Wzero are irrelevant ABAB:
> Todo: : Should allowIntersect be "false" for all SetDifference uses?

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1a3637e40923932af6f1802a1e284c3eca)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,NU1 Vzero)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, RET > `[`EWiseApply`](#namespacecombblas_1ac077b845b62f490f5b7b91526ca5b724)`(const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU1 > & V,const `[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< IU, NU2 > & W,_BinaryOperation _binary_op,_BinaryPredicate _doOp,bool allowVNulls,bool allowWNulls,NU1 Vzero,NU2 Wzero,const bool allowIntersect)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)< IU, typename [promote_trait](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< UDERA, UDERB >::T_promote > `[`Mult_AnXBn_ActiveTarget`](#namespacecombblas_1a6ba87d50b83d69c1ce209e71d8e64de2)`(const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU1, UDERA > & A,const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU2, UDERB > & B)` 

Parallel A = B*C routine that uses one-sided MPI-2 features General active target syncronization via MPI_Win_Post, MPI_Win_Start, MPI_Win_Complete, MPI_Win_Wait Tested on my dual core Macbook with 1,4,9,16,25 MPI processes No memory hog: splits the matrix into two along the column, prefetches the next half matrix while computing on the current one

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)< IU, typename [promote_trait](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< UDERA, UDERB >::T_promote > `[`Mult_AnXBn_PassiveTarget`](#namespacecombblas_1a9af27983898e812171c0def14cdd96b9)`(const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU1, UDERA > & A,const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU2, UDERB > & B)` 

Parallel A = B*C routine that uses one-sided MPI-2 features This function implements an asynchronous 2D algorithm, in the sense that there is no notion of stages. 
 The process that completes its submatrix update, requests subsequent matrices from their owners w/out waiting to sychronize with other processors 
 This partially remedies the severe load balancing problem in sparse matrices. 
 The class uses MPI-2 to achieve one-sided asynchronous communication 
 The algorithm treats each submatrix as a single block 
 Local data structure can be any [SpMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_mat) that has a constructor with array sizes and getarrs() member Passive target syncronization via MPI_Win_Lock, MPI_Win_Unlock No memory hog: splits the matrix into two along the column, prefetches the next half matrix while computing on the current one

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)< IU, typename [promote_trait](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)< NU1, NU2 >::T_promote, typename [promote_trait`](#structcombblas_1_1promote__trait)`< UDERA, UDERB >::T_promote > `[`Mult_AnXBn_Fence`](#namespacecombblas_1abda9ef69ef3c27ce08ca477ef18c977a)`(const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU1, UDERA > & A,const `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IU, NU2, UDERB > & B)` 

Parallel A = B*C routine that uses one-sided MPI-2 features Syncronization is through MPI_Win_Fence Buggy as of September, 2009

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`SpMXSpV_HeapSort`](#namespacecombblas_1acb3ff74ebde3c08da979fab30cdd8fb6)`(const `[`Csc`](#classcombblas_1_1_csc)`< IT, NT > & Acsc,int32_t mA,const int32_t * indx,const IVT * numx,int32_t veclen,std::vector< int32_t > & indy,std::vector< OVT > & numy,int32_t offset)` 

SpMXSpV with HeapSort Simply insert entries from columns corresponsing to nonzeros of the input vector into a minHeap Then extract entries from the minHeap Complexity: O(flops*log(flops)) offset is the offset of indices in the matrix in case the matrix is split This version is likely to be more memory efficient than the other one (the one that uses preallocated memory buffers) Because here we don't use a dense accumulation vector but a heap. It will probably be slower though.

Note that GenGraph500Data will return global vertex numbers (from 1... N). The ith edge can be accessed with edges[2*i] and edges[2*i+1]. There will be duplicates and the data won't be sorted. Generates an edge list consisting of an RMAT matrix suitable for the Graph500 benchmark.

#### `public void `[`CleanupEmpties`](#classcombblas_1_1_dist_edge_list_1ac1528b9f577394a710903f0abc6d424d)`()` 

Removes all edges that begin with a -1. Walks back from the end to tighten the nedges counter, then walks forward and replaces any edge with a -1 source with the last edge.

## Members

# class `combblas::FullyDist< IT, NT, typename combblas::disable_if< combblas::is_boolean< NT >::value, NT >::type >` 

The full distribution is actually a two-level distribution that matches the matrix distribution In this scheme, each processor row (except the last) is responsible for t = floor(n/sqrt(p)) elements. The last processor row gets the remaining (n-floor(n/sqrt(p))*(sqrt(p)-1)) elements Within the processor row, each processor (except the last) is responsible for loc = floor(t/sqrt(p)) elements. Example: n=103 and p=16 All processors P_ij for i=0,1,2 and j=0,1,2 get floor(floor(102/4)/4) = 6 elements All processors P_i3 for i=0,1,2 get 25-6*3 = 7 elements All processors P_3j for j=0,1,2 get (102-25*3)/4 = 6 elements Processor P_33 gets 27-6*3 = 9 elements Both derived classes, whether sparse or dense, are distributed to processors based on their "length", so that a conversion does not need any communication between sparse and dense formats

# class `combblas::FullyDistSpVec` 

```
class combblas::FullyDistSpVec
  : public combblas::FullyDist< IT, NT, combblas::disable_if< combblas::is_boolean< NT >::value, NT >::type >
```  

A sparse vector of length n (with nnz <= n of them being nonzeros) is distributed to "all the processors" in a way that "respects ordering" of the nonzero indices Example: x = [5,1,6,2,9] for nnz(x)=5 and length(x)=12 we use 4 processors P_00, P_01, P_10, P_11 Then P_00 owns [1,2](in the range [0,...,2]), P_01 ow`ns [5](in the range [3,...,5]), and so on. In the case of A(v,w) type sparse matrix indexing, this doesn't matter because n = nnz After all, A(v,w) will have dimensions length(v) x length (w) v and w will be of numerical type (NT) "int" and their indices (IT) will be consecutive integers It is possibly that nonzero counts are distributed unevenly Example: x=[1,2,3,4,5] and length(x) = 20, then P_00 would own all the nonzeros and the rest will hold empry vectors Just like in [SpParMat](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat) case, indices are local to processors (they belong to range [0,...,length-1] on each processor) Always create vectors with the right length, setting elements won't increase its length (similar to operator[] on std::vector)

#### `public `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IT, NT > `[`operator()`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec_1a87d52701801532c6bc2d575307ee6126)`(const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IT, IT > & ri) const` 

SpRef (expects ri to be 0-based)

The distribution and length are inherited from ri Its zero is inherited from *this (because ri is of type IT) Example: This is [{1,n1},{4,n4},{7,n7},{8,n8},{9,n9}] with P_00 owning {1,4} and P_11 rest Assume ri = [4,1,5,7] is distributed as two elements per processor Then result has length 4, distrubuted two element per processor, even though 5 and 7 doesn't exist This is because we are returning a "dense" output, so the absent elements will be padded with 0

#### `public void `[`SetElement`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec_1add124511e9a6271913c3f2c661afe523)`(IT indx,NT numx)` 

Indexing is performed 0-based.

# class `combblas::FullyDistVec` 

```
class combblas::FullyDistVec
  : public combblas::FullyDist< IT, NT, combblas::disable_if< combblas::is_boolean< NT >::value, NT >::type >
```

# class `combblas::Memory` 

EqualityComparable memory chunk object Two memory chunks are considered equal if either their beginaddr or the endaddr are the same (just to facilitate deallocation)

# class `combblas::MemoryPool` 

Available memory addresses will be sorted w.r.t. their starting positions 

At least one element exists in the freelist at any time. 

Defragment on the fly: at any time, NO two consecutive chunks with chunk1.endaddr equals chunk2.begaddr exist

# class `combblas::OptBuf` 

This special data structure is used for optimizing BFS iterations by providing a fixed sized buffer for communication the contents of the buffer are irrelevant until [SpImpl](#structcombblas_1_1_sp_impl):SpMXSpV starts hence the copy constructor that doesn't copy contents

#### `public  `[`SpCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_c_cols_1a7b23ce428c0b325aa0f3a6f6c3fd5717)`(const `[`SpTuples`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples)`< IT, NT > & rhs,bool transpose)` 

Constructor for converting [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) matrix -> [SpCCols](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_c_cols)
#### Parameters
* `rhs` if transpose=true, 
 then rhs is assumed to be a row sorted [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object 
 else rhs is assumed to be a column sorted [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object

The assignment operator operates on an existing object The assignment operator is the only operator that is not inherited. But there is no need to call base's assigment operator as it has no data members

#### `public  `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1a1b3e1d22eff10ac9d94699a250dd805b)`(const `[`SpTuples`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples)`< IT, NT > & rhs,bool transpose)` 

Constructor for converting [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) matrix -> [SpDCCols](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols) (may use a private memory heap) 
#### Parameters
* `rhs` if transpose=true, 
 then rhs is assumed to be a row sorted [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object 
 else rhs is assumed to be a column sorted [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object

#### `public  `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1a09d21a48e65de6d86ce48c3145a62d2b)`(IT nRow,IT nCol,IT nnz1,const std::tuple< IT, IT, NT > * rhs,bool transpose)` 

Multithreaded Constructor for converting tuples matrix -> [SpDCCols](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)
#### Parameters
* `rhs` if transpose=true, 
 then tuples is assumed to be a row sorted list of tuple objects 
 else tuples is assumed to be a column sorted list of tuple objects

#### `public inline void `[`RowSplit`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1acb9aea74ac685ea21b775577fb84b54d)`(int numsplits)` 

#### `public void `[`ColSplit`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1a25d36b176464f53ffc803542e8682660)`(int parts,std::vector< `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IT, NT > > & matrices)` 

> Destroys calling object (*this)

Splits the matrix into "parts", simply by cutting along the columns Simple algorithm that doesn't intend to split perfectly, but it should do a pretty good job Practically destructs the calling object also (frees most of its memory)

#### `public void `[`ColConcatenate`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1a3bbe4765106a735fda79d419191492d1)`(std::vector< `[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IT, NT > > & matrices)` 

> Destroys its parameters (matrices)

Concatenates (merges) multiple matrices (cut along the columns) into 1 piece [ColSplit()](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1a25d36b176464f53ffc803542e8682660) method should have been executed on the object beforehand

#### `public void `[`Split`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols_1af448cdcc975b88774501a00ab29ed5da)`(`[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IT, NT > & partA,`[`SpDCCols`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_d_c_cols)`< IT, NT > & partB)` 

> Destroys calling object (*this)

Splits the matrix into two parts, simply by cutting along the columns Simple algorithm that doesn't intend to split perfectly, but it should do a pretty good job Practically destructs the calling object also (frees most of its memory) 
> Todo: {special case of ColSplit, to be deprecated...}

# class `combblas::SpHelper` 

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------

## Members

# class `combblas::SpMat` 

The abstract base class for all derived sequential sparse matrix classes Contains no data members, hence no copy constructor/assignment operator Uses static polymorphism through curiously recurring templates (CRTP) Template parameters: IT (index type), NT (numerical type), DER (derived class type)

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------
`public inline void `[`Create`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_mat_1aec83f0568245560ac797cbf181c47051)`(const std::vector< IT > & essentials)` | Standard destructor, copy ctor and assignment are generated by compiler, they all do nothing ! Default constructor also exists, and does nothing more than creating Base<Derived>() and Derived() objects One has to call one of the overloaded create functions to get an nonempty object

#### `public inline void `[`Create`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_mat_1aec83f0568245560ac797cbf181c47051)`(const std::vector< IT > & essentials)` 

Standard destructor, copy ctor and assignment are generated by compiler, they all do nothing ! Default constructor also exists, and does nothing more than creating Base<Derived>() and Derived() objects One has to call one of the overloaded create functions to get an nonempty object

# class `combblas::SpParHelper` 

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------

## Members

# class `combblas::SpParMat` 

Fundamental 2D distributed sparse matrix class The index type IT is encapsulated by the class in a way that it is only guarantee that the implementation will ensure the requested semantics. For instance, if IT=int64 then the implementation can still use 32 bit local indices but it should return correct 64-bit numbers in its functions. In other words, DER can be SpDCCols<int32_t, double> while IT=int64_t

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`bool `[`Kselect`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a866b8dd43a9b9bcb1f9d3415fb6649b2)`(`[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< GIT, VT > & kth,IT k_limit,int kselectVersion) const` 

Kselect wrapper for a select columns of the matrix Indices of the input sparse vectors kth denote the queried columns of the matrix Upon return, values of kth stores the kth entries of the queried columns Returns true if Kselect algorithm is invoked for at least one column Otherwise, returns false

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`bool `[`Kselect1`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a5a93ec81a4fef154e4c81d587ef70088)`(`[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< GIT, VT > & rvec,IT k_limit) const` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`bool `[`Kselect2`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a099b555ec322be6ebfa71980dff01ba2)`(`[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< GIT, VT > & rvec,IT k_limit) const` 

identify the k-th maximum element in each column of a matrix if the number of nonzeros in a column is less than k, return the numeric_limits<NT>::min() This is an efficient implementation of the Saukas/Song algorithm [http://www.ime.usp.br/~einar/select/INDEX.HTM](http://www.ime.usp.br/~einar/select/INDEX.HTM) Preferred for large k values

#### `public IT `[`Profile`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a900bd026794dc593bcfcbd9ef5c9396d)`() const` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`MaskedReduce`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a4e77be9cddbacc0ff697580b111f865b)`(`[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< GIT, VT > & rvec,`[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< GIT, VT > & mask,`[`Dim`](#namespacecombblas_1a06c6e69e44c7f7c611814444dcb55ba0)` dim,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,VT id,bool exclude) const` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`MaskedReduce`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1ae7fcc457e1a672fbe0aef364947c8ced)`(`[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< GIT, VT > & rvec,`[`FullyDistSpVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_sp_vec)`< GIT, VT > & mask,`[`Dim`](#namespacecombblas_1a06c6e69e44c7f7c611814444dcb55ba0)` dim,_BinaryOperation __binary_op,VT id,_UnaryOperation __unary_op,bool exclude) const` 

Reduce along the column into a vector 
#### Parameters
* `mask` {A sparse vector indicating row indices included/excluded (based on exclude argument) in the reduction } 

* `__binary_op` {the operation used for reduction; examples: max, min, plus, multiply, and, or. Its parameters and return type are all VT} 

* `id` {scalar that is used as the identity for __binary_op; examples: zero, infinity} 

* `__unary_op` {optional unary operation applied to nonzeros *before* the __binary_op; examples: 1/x, x^2} 

* `exclude` {if true, masked row indices are included in the reduction} 

* `rvec` {the return vector, specified as an output parameter to allow arbitrary return types via VT}

#### `public `[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IT, NT, DER > `[`SubsRefCol`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a3072ff5e8fe858614f7c96c24c5ddeb1)`(const std::vector< IT > & ci) const` 

Column indexing with special parallel semantics.

Create a submatrix of size m x (size(ci) * s) on a r x s processor grid Essentially fetches the columns ci[0], ci[1],... ci[size(ci)] from every submatrix

#### `public template<>`  <br/>[`SpParMat`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat)`< IT, NT, DER > `[`SubsRef_SR`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_par_mat_1a758a7e03ab30a516d7e7f045b1c3459e)`(const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IT, IT > & ri,const `[`FullyDistVec`](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec)`< IT, IT > & ci,bool inplace)` 

General indexing with serial semantics.

Generalized sparse matrix indexing (ri/ci are 0-based indexed) Both the storage and the actual values in [FullyDistVec](#classcombblas_1_1_fully_dist_vec) should be IT The index vectors are dense and FULLY distributed on all processors We can use this function to apply a permutation like A(p,q) Sequential indexing subroutine (via multiplication) is general enough.

# class `combblas::SpTuples` 

```
class combblas::SpTuples
  : public combblas::SpMat< IT, NT, SpTuples< IT, NT > >
```  

Triplets are represented using the boost::tuple class of the Boost library Number of entries are 64-bit addressible, but each entry is only <class it>=""> addressible Therefore, size is int64_t but nrows/ncols (representing range of first two entries in tuple) is of type IT Indices start from 0 in this class 

Sorted with respect to columns (Column-sorted triples)

#### `public  `[`SpTuples`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples_1a9bb84fd94c8648e6bbc12c49ae303535)`(`[`int64_t`](#compat_8h_1a312c7e8848187d110315ab83a7b3d4d0)` maxnnz,IT nRow,IT nCol,std::vector< IT > & edges,bool removeloops)` 

Generate a [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object from an edge list 
#### Parameters
* `edges` edge list that might contain duplicate edges. freed upon return Semantics differ depending on the object created: NT=bool: duplicates are ignored NT='countable' (such as short,int): duplicated as summed to keep count

#### `public  `[`SpTuples`](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples_1a99417b0c3215c8a4c97dfaba9319a021)`(`[`int64_t`](#compat_8h_1a312c7e8848187d110315ab83a7b3d4d0)` size,IT nRow,IT nCol,`[`StackEntry`](#classcombblas_1_1_stack_entry)`< NT, std::pair< IT, IT > > *& multstack)` 

Generate a [SpTuples](#classcombblas_1_1_sp_tuples) object from [StackEntry](#classcombblas_1_1_stack_entry) array, then delete that array 
#### Parameters
* `multstack` {value-key pairs where keys are pair<col_ind, row_ind> sorted lexicographically} 

Since input is column sorted, the tuples are automatically generated in that way too

# struct `combblas::bitwise_and` 

```
struct combblas::bitwise_and
  : public std::binary_function< T, T, T >
```  

Compute the bitwise AND of two integral values.

This binary function object computes the bitwise AND of the two values it is given. When used with MPI and a type `T` that has an associated, built-in MPI data type, translates to `MPI_BAND`.

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------
`public inline T `[`operator()`](#structcombblas_1_1bitwise__and_1a41ae501d329e5e0fcb60699860f2c03b)`(const T & x,const T & y) const` | #### Returns

## Members

#### `public inline T `[`operator()`](#structcombblas_1_1bitwise__and_1a41ae501d329e5e0fcb60699860f2c03b)`(const T & x,const T & y) const` 

#### Returns
`x` & y.

# struct `combblas::exponentiate` 

```
struct combblas::exponentiate
  : public std::binary_function< double, double, double >
```  

binary_function<Arg1, Arg2, Result> This is left untemplated because pow() only makes sense for <double, int, double> , <double, double, double> , <float, float, float> and C++ can automatically upcast each case to <double, double, double>

# struct `combblas::logical_xor` 

```
struct combblas::logical_xor
  : public std::binary_function< T, T, T >
```  

Compute the logical exclusive OR of two integral values.

This binary function object computes the logical exclusive of the two values it is given. When used with MPI and a type `T` that has an associated, built-in MPI data type, translates to `MPI_LXOR`.

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------
`public inline T `[`operator()`](#structcombblas_1_1logical__xor_1ad764e97f29606506c14cc58424de9928)`(const T & x,const T & y) const` | #### Returns

## Members

#### `public inline T `[`operator()`](#structcombblas_1_1logical__xor_1ad764e97f29606506c14cc58424de9928)`(const T & x,const T & y) const` 

#### Returns
the logical exclusive OR of x and y.

# struct `combblas::SpImpl` 

IT: The sparse matrix index type. Sparse vector index type is fixed to be int32_t It is the caller function's (inside ParFriends/Friends) job to convert any different types and ensure correctness. Rationale is efficiency, and the fact that we know for sure that 32-bit LOCAL indices are sufficient for all reasonable concurrencies and data sizes (as of 2011) 
> Todo: : As of 2015, this might not be true!!! (ABAB)

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions

`public template<>`  <br/>`int `[`sampleSort`](#namespacepar_1a5e83521778f7e9a2d44f46f1eadaad92)`(std::vector< T > & in,std::vector< T > & out,MPI_Comm comm)`            | A parallel sample sort implementation. In our implementation, we do not pose any restriction on the input or the number of processors. This function can be used with an odd number of processors as well. Some processors can pass an empty vector as input. If the total number of elements in the vector (globally) is fewer than 10*p^2, where p is the number of processors, then we will use bitonic sort instead of sample sort to sort the vector. We use a paralle bitonic sort to sort the samples in the sample sort algorithm. Hence, the complexity of the algorithm is O(n/p log n/p) + O(p log p). Here, n is the global length of the vector and p is the number of processors.

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`int `[`HyperQuickSort_cav`](#namespacepar_1a7f1047ce25b4fa30fcf2f5d5cc85176a)`(std::vector< T > & in,MPI_Comm comm)` 

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`int `[`sampleSort`](#namespacepar_1a5e83521778f7e9a2d44f46f1eadaad92)`(std::vector< T > & in,std::vector< T > & out,MPI_Comm comm)` 

A parallel sample sort implementation. In our implementation, we do not pose any restriction on the input or the number of processors. This function can be used with an odd number of processors as well. Some processors can pass an empty vector as input. If the total number of elements in the vector (globally) is fewer than 10*p^2, where p is the number of processors, then we will use bitonic sort instead of sample sort to sort the vector. We use a paralle bitonic sort to sort the samples in the sample sort algorithm. Hence, the complexity of the algorithm is O(n/p log n/p) + O(p log p). Here, n is the global length of the vector and p is the number of processors.

Hari Sundar 

#### Parameters
* `in` the input vector 

* `out` the output vector 

* `comm` the communicator

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`int `[`sampleSort`](#namespacepar_1afdfbd6cd3f7a7f6af7501df91738c8b8)`(std::vector< T > & in,MPI_Comm comm)`

Splits a communication group into two, one containing processors that passed a value of 'false' for the parameter 'iAmEmpty' and the another containing processors that passed a value of 'true' for the parameter. Both the groups are sorted in the ascending order of their ranks in the old comm.

Rahul Sampath 

#### Parameters

* `orig_comm` The comm group that needs to be split. 

* `new_comm` The new comm group.

Rahul Sampath

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`MergeLists`](#namespacepar_1ae3b8391c3ddda3ceea327c8f4df32b0e)`(std::vector< T > & listA,std::vector< T > & listB,int KEEP_WHAT)` 

Merges lists A, and B, retaining either the low or the High in list A.

Hari Sundar 

#### Parameters
* `listA` Input list, and where the output is stored. 

* `listB` Second input list. 

* `KEEP_WHAT` determines whether to retain the High or the low values from A and B. One of KEEP_HIGH or KEEP_LOW.

Merging the two lists when their sizes are not the same is a bit involved. The major condition that needs to be used is that all elements that are less than max(min(A), min(B)) are retained by the KEEP_LOW processor, and similarly all elements that are larger larger than min(max(A), max(B)) are retained by the KEEP_HIGH processor.

The reason for this is that, on the Keep_Low side,

max(min(A), min(B)) > min(A) > max(A-)

and similarly on the Keep_high side,

min(max(A), max(B)) < max(A) < min(A+)

which guarantees that the merged lists remain bitonic.

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`MergeSplit`](#namespacepar_1abad721e799fda8d9b03f005c82dfd907)`(std::vector< T > & local_list,int which_keys,int partner,MPI_Comm comm)` 

The main operation in the parallel bitonic sort algorithm. This implements the compare-split operation.

Hari Sundar 

#### Parameters
* `which_keys` is one of KEEP_HIGH or KEEP_LOW 

* `partner` is the processor with which to Merge and Split. 

* `local_list` the input vector 

* `comm` the communicator

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`Par_bitonic_sort_incr`](#namespacepar_1a88e164ad279018147554138bbb8716c6)`(std::vector< T > & local_list,int proc_set_size,MPI_Comm comm)` 

Hari Sundar

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`Par_bitonic_sort_decr`](#namespacepar_1aa5681739fc044d4774f199186027bc82)`(std::vector< T > & local_list,int proc_set_size,MPI_Comm comm)` 

Hari Sundar

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`Par_bitonic_merge_incr`](#namespacepar_1a63eb714a90c5cf391b0c37baa804644c)`(std::vector< T > & local_list,int proc_set_size,MPI_Comm comm)` 

Hari Sundar

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`bitonicSort_binary`](#namespacepar_1a0e3992a13172d29616c6d877d283178c)`(std::vector< T > & in,MPI_Comm comm)` 

An implementation of parallel bitonic sort that expects the number of processors to be a power of 2. However, unlike most implementations, we do not expect the length of the vector (neither locally nor globally) to be a power of 2 or even. Moreover, each processor can call this with a different number of elements. However, we do expect that 'in' atleast has 1 element on each processor.

#### Parameters
* `in` the vector to be sorted 

Hari Sundar

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`bitonicSort`](#namespacepar_1a41724fba006b22060f83b15d96e81e5b)`(std::vector< T > & in,MPI_Comm comm)` 

An implementation of parallel bitonic sort that does not expect the number of processors to be a power of 2. In fact, the number of processors can even be odd. Moreover, we do not even expect the length of the vector (neither locally nor globally) to be a power of 2 or even. Moreover, each processor can call this with a different number of elements. However, we do expect that 'in' atleast has 1 element on each processor. This recursively calls the function bitonicSort_binary, followed by a special parallel merge.

#### Parameters
* `in` the vector to be sorted 

Hari Sundar 

**See also**: [bitonicSort_binary](#namespacepar_1a0e3992a13172d29616c6d877d283178c)

#### `public int `[`AdjustCommunicationPattern`](#namespacepar_1a6a19f62e00209e39193f28049bb305b5)`(std::vector< int > & send_sizes,std::vector< int > & send_partners,std::vector< int > & recv_sizes,std::vector< int > & recv_partners,MPI_Comm comm)` 

# class `par::Mpi_datatype` 

An abstract class used for communicating messages using user-defined datatypes. The user must implement the static member function "value()" that returns the MPI_Datatype corresponding to this user-defined datatype.

Hari Sundar, [hsundar@gmail.com](mailto:hsundar@gmail.com)

**See also**: [Mpi_datatype<bool>](#classpar_1_1_mpi__datatype_3_01bool_01_4)

## Members

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`flashsort`](#namespaceseq_1a0ffdcb61e596e75de51b49ad995478d0)`(T * a,int n,int m,int * ctr)` 

Flash sort algo to sort an array in O(n).

#### Parameters
* `a` The array to be sorted 

* `n` The number of elements in a 

* `m` Size of index vector. typically m = 0.1*n 

* `ctr` The number of times flashsort was called.

Sorts array a with n elements by use of the index vector l of dimension m (with m about 0.1 n). The routine runs fastest with a uniform distribution of elements. The vector l is declare dynamically using the calloc function. The variable ctr counts the number of times that flashsort is called. THRESHOLD is a very important constant. It is the minimum number of elements required in a subclass before recursion is used.

Templated version of flashsort based on original C code by Karl-Dietrich Neubert.

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`void `[`makeVectorUnique`](#namespaceseq_1a24884a2eced0b8dce24a50a2d224877b)`(std::vector< T > & vec,bool isSorted)` 

Removes duplicates from the vector.

Rahul Sampath 

#### Parameters
* `vec` The vector to be made free of duplicates. 

* `isSorted` Pass 'true' if the input is sorted.

If the vector is not sorted, it is first sorted before removing duplicates.

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`bool `[`BinarySearch`](#namespaceseq_1a9e6ce94b3ad83bb2dda2cfb7db4b4931)`(const T * arr,unsigned int nelem,const T & key,unsigned int * idx)` 

A binary search implementation.

Rahul Sampath 

#### Parameters
* `arr` A sorted array 

* `nelem` The length of the array 

* `key` The search key 

* `idx` 0-based index of the position of the key in the array 

#### Returns
'true' if the key exists in the array and 'false' otherwise

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`int `[`UpperBound`](#namespaceseq_1a6a2cb0cb782ebbb6879b2bc72b9034e7)`(unsigned int nelem,const T * arr,unsigned int startIdx,const T & key)` 

Finds the index of the smallest upper bound of the search key in the array.

Santi Swaroop Adavani 

#### Parameters
* `arr` A sorted array 

* `nelem` The length of the array 

* `startIdx` The starting location to search from 

* `key` The search key 

#### Returns
the index of the first element in the array >= key

#### `public template<>`  <br/>`bool `[`maxLowerBound`](#namespaceseq_1af1891a3ddf195111c4ce3b8346ec60a6)`(const std::vector< T > & arr,const T & key,unsigned int & retIdx,unsigned int * leftIdx,unsigned int * rightIdx)` 

Finds the index of the greatest lower bound of the search key in the array. The implementation uses a simple modification of the binary search algorithm.

Rahul Sampath 

#### Parameters
* `arr` A sorted array 

* `key` The search key 

* `retIdx` The index of the position of the last element in the array <= key 

* `leftIdx` If this is not NULL, then the search will be limited to elements at positions >= *leftIdx 

* `rightIdx` if this is not NULL, then the search will be limited to elements at positions <= *rightIdx 

#### Returns
'true' if the search was successful

# class `TwitterEdge` 

This is not part of the Combinatorial BLAS library, it's just an example. A nonzero A(i,j) is present if at least one edge (of any type) from vertex i to vertex j exists. Multiple types of edges are supported: follower/retweeter (or both)

# struct `LatestRetwitterBFS` 

Filters are only indirectly supported in Combinatorial BLAS KDT generates them by embedding their filter stack and pushing those predicates to the [SR::multiply()](#namespacecombblas_1aa41745887d93f0f543679c468548373e) function, conceptually like if(predicate(maxrix_val)) { bin_op(xxx) } Here we emulate this filtered traversal approach.

# struct `prunediscovered`

struct prunediscovered
  : public std::binary_function< int64_t, int64_t, int64_t >
  : public std::binary_function< int64_t, int64_t, int64_t >
  : public std::binary_function< int64_t, int64_t, int64_t >

# struct `tommy_chain_struct` 

Chain of nodes. A chain of nodes is a sequence of nodes with the following properties:

* It contains at least one node. A chains of zero nodes cannot exist.

* The next field of the tail is of *undefined* value.

* The prev field of the head is of *undefined* value.

* All the other inner prev and next fields are correctly set.

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------

`public `[`tommy_node`](#tommytypes_8h_1a56a5b6211015e83fd69c4f990ac5612b)` * `[`tail`](#structtommy__chain__struct_1ae0fe33060c36743174cdeb948781853f) | Pointer at the tail of the chain.

# struct `tommy_node_struct` 

Data structure node. This node type is shared between all the data structures and used to store some info directly into the objects you want to store.

A typical declaration is: 
```cpp
struct object {
    tommy_node node;
    // other fields
};
```

## Summary

 Members                        | Descriptions                                
--------------------------------|---------------------------------------------
`public struct `[`tommy_node_struct`](#structtommy__node__struct)` * `[`next`](#structtommy__node__struct_1a53338f3f5366866598ed9ac7e46e64a2) | Next node. The tail node has it at 0, like a 0 terminated list.
`public struct `[`tommy_node_struct`](#structtommy__node__struct)` * `[`prev`](#structtommy__node__struct_1a5f5ffba676428636553612ddd809443c) | Previous node. The head node points to the tail node, like a circular list.
`public void * `[`data`](#structtommy__node__struct_1a6210792ec52fa1efbfb44cf4557d9b6f) | Pointer at the object containing the node. This field is initialized when inserting nodes into a data structure.
`public `[`tommy_key_t`](#tommytypes_8h_1a8812c3379df4aaf65a3605a22faf4787)` `[`key`](#structtommy__node__struct_1a124aaecab9e5d3d1fbb9239dac779d23) | Key used to store the node. With hashtables this field is used to store the hash value. With lists this field is not used.
